- The mass defect refers to the fact that the mass of an element's nucleus weighs slightly less than the sum of its protons and neutrons. -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 38 of 59 / search: "number of protons and neutrons in the nucleus"
- The strong nuclear force is a fundamental force that draws protons & neutrons toward each other when they're brought into close proximity. -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 38 of 59 / search: "nuclear protons neutrons"; 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 5 of 5 / search: "strong close proximity"
- "In alpha decay, α-particles are packets of helium atoms - containing 2 protons and 2 neutrons." -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 38 of 59 / search: "decay particles protons"
- "In beta- decay, the atomic numbers (Z) of daughter nuclei are +1 & the mass numbers (A) are unchanged." -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 38 of 59 / search: "beta decay atomic"
- In beta- decay, a neutron is converted into a proton - emitting a(n) electron & anti-neutrino. -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 38 of 59 / search: "beta decay converted"
- In beta+ decay, a proton is converted into a neutron - emitting a(n) positron & neutrino. -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 38 of 59 / search: "beta decay converted"
- "In gamma decay, the atomic numbers (Z) of daughter nuclei are unchanged & the mass numbers (A) are unchanged." -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 38 of 59 / search: "gamma decay atomic"
- Gamma decay is when excited parent nuclei relieve themselves of energy by emitting high-energy γ-rays (photons). -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 38 of 59 / search: "gamma decay excited"
- beta+ decay is also called positron emission. -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 38 of 59 / search: "beta decay emission"
- In the different types of nuclear decay, atomic changes happen simultaneously with the emission of electromagnetic waves, gamma rays, as radiation. -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 38 of 59 / search: "nuclear decay atomic"; 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 37 of 59 / search: "electromagnetic rays radiation"

- Charges of these nuclear decay particles... alpha particle: positively charged beta+ particle: positively charged (positron) beta- particle: negatively charged (electron) gamma particle: neutral -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 38 of 59 / search: "nuclear decay particles"; 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 10 of 59 / search: "positively charged beta"; 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 45 of 59 / search: "charges particles particle"

- For magnetic fields acting on negative charges, use the left-hand rule. -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 45 of 59 / search: "acting charges left"

- In magnetic fields, the magnetic field lines are perpendicular to the direction of the magnetic force (FM). -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 36 of 59 / search: "magnetic fields field"

## Psychology - Disorders.txt

- Biomedical vs. Biopsychosocial model for treating mental disorders: Biomedical: focuses on the biology/biochemistry of the disorder. Biopsychosocial: considers biological, psychological factors that might cause it. -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 7 of 30 / search: "biomedical model psychological"
- Biomedical vs. Biopsychosocial model for treating mental disorders: Biopsychosocial: considers biological, psychological factors that might cause it. Biomedical: focuses on the biology/biochemistry of the disorder. -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 7 of 30 / search: "biomedical model psychological"
- Bipolar disorders are characterized by periods of mania followed by depressive episodes. -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 6 of 30 / search: "bipolar periods mania"; 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 4 of 30 / search: "bipolar periods mania"; 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 5 of 30 / search: "bipolar periods mania"

- Stressor-related disorders are mental disorders brought on after a traumatic event. -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 8 of 30 / search: "exposure to a traumatic event and is characterized"
- Compulsions for individuals with OCD are the specific rituals they perform in response to obsessive thoughts. -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 13 of 59 / search: "ocd rituals obsessive"; 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 14 of 59 / search: "ocd rituals obsessive"; 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 15 of 59 / search: "ocd rituals obsessive"
- Somatic symptom disorders are characterized by extreme concern regarding the physical symptoms of one's health. -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 3 of 20 / search: "somatic symptom extreme concern regarding one or more"
- Genetic predispositions to depression work by increasing your likelihood to develop adverse emotional responses to trauma. -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 9 of 30 / search: "depression work emotional"; 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 22 of 30 / search: "depression work emotional"; 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 25 of 30 / search: "depression work emotional"

- Conversion disorder is when people experience real neurological symptoms that cannot be explained by an underlying medical condition. -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 3 of 20 / search: "conversion neurological condition"

## Psychology - Drugs Biology.txt

- Depressants, stimulants, and hallucinogens are psychoactive drugs. -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 15 of 15 / search: "usually opiates depressants stimulants and hallucinogens sedatives eg"
- Both barbituates & benzodiazepines depress the CNS to make you less anxious & more tired. -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 15 of 15 / search: "benzodiazepines depress cns"
- Benzodiazepines depress the CNS by making more Cl- channels for GABA to bind to. -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 15 of 15 / search: "benzodiazepines depress cns"
- Psychomotor stimulants are drugs that stimulate the CNS by acting as dopamine agonists. -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 15 of 15 / search: "stimulants drugs cns"
- How barbituates & benzodiazepines work... Barbituates: depress the CNS by causing excess Cl- influx. Benzodiazepines: depress the CNS by creating more Cl- channels for GABA. -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 15 of 15 / search: "benzodiazepines depress cns"
- How barbituates & benzodiazepines work... Benzodiazepines: depress the CNS by creating more Cl- channels for GABA. Barbituates: depress the CNS by causing excess Cl- influx. -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 15 of 15 / search: "benzodiazepines depress cns"

## Psychology - Memory.txt

- The primacy & recency effects are collectively called the serial position effect. -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 14 of 30 / search: "primacy recency serial"
- The primacy effect says we'll remember information towards the beginning of a list easier than the middle. -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 14 of 30 / search: "primacy remember beginning"
- The recency effect says we'll remember information towards the end of a list easier than the middle. -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 14 of 30 / search: "recency remember list"
- Flashbulb memories are extremely vivid memories that feel real. -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 20 of 30 / search: "flashbulb memories extremely"
- The hippocampus & amygdala are located in the temporal lobe, which means the temporal lobe is crucial for memory & emotional processing. -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 24 of 30 / search: "hippocampus located emotional"
- Short-term memory is memory for an event that occurred less than 20 seconds ago. -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 7 of 20 / search: "information in short term memory which has a"
- The primacy effect relies on long-term memory, and the recency effect relies on short-term memory. -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 7 of 20 / search: "information in short term memory which has a"
- The recency effect relies on short-term memory, and the primacy effect relies on long-term memory. -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 7 of 20 / search: "information in short term memory which has a"
- Retroactive interference relies on information stored in your short-term memory. -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 7 of 20 / search: "information in short term memory which has a"
- The Atkinson-Shiffrin model of memory is an alternative to the typical Baddley model, which says the 3 components of our memory are... 1. Sensory memory store 2. Short-term memory store 3. Long-term memory store -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 7 of 20 / search: "information in short term memory which has a"
- The amygdala is involved in the formation of highly emotional memories into long-term memory. -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 20 of 30 / search: "emotional memories term"
- In order for the serial position effect to take place, the recall task must be given immedietly after presenting the words. -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 7 of 20 / search: "recall task words"
- If researchers studying the serial position effect waited 20 minutes to administer the recall task after presenting the words, they'd see a disappearance of the recency effect, since that relies entirely on short-term memory. -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 7 of 20 / search: "information in short term memory which has a"; 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 20 of 30 / search: "studying minutes short"; 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 14 of 30 / search: "serial recall recency"
- People are better able to recall the central details of flashbulb memories while forgetting the peripheral details, since increased emotional arousal shifts our focus onto the event's central features. -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 20 of 30 / search: "recall details flashbulb"; 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 58 of 59 / search: "peripheral since features"

## Psychology - Personality.txt

- Psychoanalytic theory of personality says our behavior is shaped by our unconscious thoughts. -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 10 of 10 / search: "psychoanalytic personality says"; 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 1 of 20 / search: "psychoanalytic personality unconscious"; 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 6 of 30 / search: "personality behavior thoughts"

- The idea of the self-concept belongs to the humanistic theory of personality. -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 10 of 30 / search: "self concept personality"
- According to the humanistic theory, our self-concept is the set of perceptions we have about ourselves. -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 10 of 30 / search: "perceptions on self concept is not explored in"
- The humanistic theory of personality believes we feel fulfillment when our behaviors align with our self-concept. -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 10 of 30 / search: "personality self concept"
- Operant conditioning uses rewards & punishments to reinforce certain behaviors. -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 19 of 30 / search: "operant conditioning uses"
- Mirror neurons are essential in observational learning. -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 6 of 20 / search: "central role in observational learning passage 1 questions"

- Defense mechanisms are classified into 4 major categories: pathological, mature, immature, & neurotic. -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 1 of 20 / search: "psychoanalytic theory defense mechanisms are the largely unconscious"; 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 10 of 10 / search: "psychoanalytic theory defense mechanisms are the largely unconscious"

- In defense mechanisms, projection & passive aggression are categorized as a immature mechanisms. -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 1 of 20 / search: "defense mechanisms projection"; 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 10 of 10 / search: "defense mechanisms projection"

- In neurotic defense mechanisms, rationalization is when you make excuses for your behaviors in order to cope. -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 1 of 20 / search: "defense mechanisms rationalization"; 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 10 of 10 / search: "defense mechanisms you"
- In neurotic defense mechanisms, repression is when you unintenionally bury thoughts to your unconscious. -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 10 of 10 / search: "defense mechanisms you"; 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 1 of 20 / search: "defense mechanisms thoughts"
- In neurotic defense mechanisms, displacement is when you take out your anger on someone/something else. -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 1 of 20 / search: "defense mechanisms displacement"; 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 10 of 10 / search: "defense mechanisms you"
- In mature defense mechanisms, suppression is when you intentionally bury thoughts to your unconscious. -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 10 of 10 / search: "defense mechanisms you"; 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 1 of 20 / search: "defense mechanisms thoughts"
- Mirror neurons are the most active in the motor cortex, somatosensory cortex, and pre-frontal cortex. -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 6 of 20 / search: "mirror neurons frontal"
- Defense mechanisms are carried out by the ego. -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 1 of 20 / search: "psychoanalytic theory defense mechanisms are the largely unconscious"; 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 10 of 10 / search: "psychoanalytic theory defense mechanisms are the largely unconscious"
- Another name for the general phenomenon of observational learning is modeling. -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 6 of 20 / search: "observational learning modeling"; 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 3 of 30 / search: "the process of observational learning see 18 1"
- According to Adler's theory of personality, our personality is shaped by feelings of inferiority and how those feelings impact our need for self-assertion. -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 6 of 30 / search: "personality feelings self"; 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 10 of 30 / search: "personality shaped self"

## Psychology - Self Identity.txt

- The existential component of our self-concept is our ability realize that we exist as distinct entities separate from others. -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 10 of 30 / search: "perceptions on self concept is not explored in"
- The categorical component of our self-concept is how we categorize ourselves according to our age, gender, skill-set, etc. -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 10 of 30 / search: "perceptions on self concept is not explored in"
- According to Carl Rogers on the self-concept, our self-image is the view we have of ourselves. -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 8 of 30 / search: "self image view"
- According to the social identity theory, our self-concept has two components: our personal identity & our social identity. -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 10 of 30 / search: "identity self concept"
- Individuals with a weak self-efficacy focus on their own personal failures and avoid challenges. -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 9 of 30 / search: "self own failures"
- According to Albert Bandura, psychological responses are ways we can increase our self-efficacy by learning how to control our emotions. -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 8 of 10 / search: "self learning emotions"
- Freud proposed the psychosexual theory to describe the stages of our personality development. -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 10 of 30 / search: "psychosexual stages personality"
- Stages of the psychosexual theory of personality development: Oral → anal → phallic → latent → genital -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 10 of 30 / search: "stages psychosexual personality"
- In Freud's psychosexual theory, children move beyond the phallic phase once they adopt similar characteristics as the same-sex parent. -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 28 of 30 / search: "phase characteristics sex"; 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 30 of 30 / search: "phase characteristics sex"
- In Erikson's psychosocial theory, individuals in identity vs. role confusion begin to develop their own self-identity. -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 9 of 30 / search: "identity own self"; 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 10 of 30 / search: "identity begin self"
- In Vygotsky's sociocultural cognitive theory, the 3 needed components for progression from elementary → higher mental functioning: 1. MKO (more knowledgeable other) instructs student. 2. Difficulty of tasks given within zone of proximal development. 3. Lang... -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 4 of 20 / search: "functioning difficulty language"
- Charles Cooley believed our self-identities are shaped through the social interactions with everyone we meet in our lives. -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 10 of 30 / search: "self identities shaped"
- Mead believed our self-identities are shaped through the social interactions with only certain people in our lives. -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 10 of 30 / search: "self identities shaped"
- Mead developed social behaviorism to explain how our self-identities are shaped through social interaction. -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 10 of 30 / search: "self identities shaped"
- Mead's idea of the Me is our non-spontaneous self that reflects how we believe society expects us to act. -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 16 of 20 / search: "idea spontaneous self"

## Psychology - Sensation.txt

- Size constancy is knowing two objects are the same size despite the closer one appearing larger. -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 1 of 10 / search: "size constancy despite"
- Color constancy is when we recognize an object is the same color despite changes in lighting. -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 1 of 10 / search: "color constancy despite"

We perceive... water feels hot → water stops feeling hot. -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 12 of 59 / search: "hands become feels"; 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 13 of 59 / search: "hands become feels"; 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 14 of 59 / search: "hands become feels"
- In sensory adaptation, how does our sense of smell adapt to odors? Sensory receptors in our nose becomes desensitized to the odor molecules - eventually stop being able to smell it. -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 9 of 10 / search: "sensory adaptation odor"

Their eyes eventually adapted to the goggles and flipped vision back to the proper orientation. -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 9 of 10 / search: "sensory adaptation vision"

## Psychology - Sleep Consciousness.txt

## Psychology - Vision.txt

- The retina contains both rods and cones. Where are the rods & cones located (respectively) on the retina? On the retina... Center: cones Periphery: rods -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 24 of 30 / search: "retina located center"
- In the eye, the fovea is dimpled inward. What benefit does this serve? Allows light to come into direct contact with cones instead of having to pass through nerve axons -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 3 of 6 / search: "not in direct contact with the surrounding environment"
- The bipolar cells that transmit information from our rods & cones are supported by horizontal cells, which help detect visual contrasts. -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 2 of 10 / search: "our detect visual"
- The optic tracts carry signals from the optic nerve past the optic chiasma to reach the brain. -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 7 of 10 / search: "tracts carry reach"
- Parvocellular & magnocellular cells are located in the lateral geniculate nucleus in the thalamus. -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 18 of 30 / search: "center called the lateral geniculate nucleus lgn in"; 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 19 of 30 / search: "center called the lateral geniculate nucleus lgn in"; 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 20 of 30 / search: "center called the lateral geniculate nucleus lgn in"
- Feature detection refers to how only particular neurons fire in response to certain stimuli (visual, auditory, etc.) in order for us to process them. -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 9 of 10 / search: "feature detection neurons"; 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 4 of 10 / search: "detection visual auditory"
- In the parvocellular pathway, signals from the retina travel to the lateral geniculate nucleus → primary visual cortex → anterior of cortex. -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 18 of 30 / search: "center called the lateral geniculate nucleus lgn in"; 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 19 of 30 / search: "center called the lateral geniculate nucleus lgn in"; 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 20 of 30 / search: "center called the lateral geniculate nucleus lgn in"
- In the magnocellular pathway, signals from the retina travel to the lateral geniculate nucleus → primary visual cortex → posterior of cortex. -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 18 of 30 / search: "center called the lateral geniculate nucleus lgn in"; 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 19 of 30 / search: "center called the lateral geniculate nucleus lgn in"; 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 20 of 30 / search: "center called the lateral geniculate nucleus lgn in"
- Visual information from an object in our right or left field of vision is processed in both hemisphere(s). -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 28 of 30 / search: "visual left field"
- Visual information from the right-side components of the object in each right and left visual field are processed in the left hemisphere. -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 28 of 30 / search: "the patients left visual field he is unable"; 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 5 of 20 / search: "the body the left hemisphere controls touch and"
- Visual information from the left-side components of the object in each right and left visual field are processed in the right hemisphere. -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 28 of 30 / search: "the patients left visual field he is unable"

## Psychology.txt

- The person-situation controversy is a controversy that stems from a disagreement about the degree to which a person's reaction to a situation is due to either their personality or the situation itself. -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 8 of 30 / search: "person situation personality"
- Empty nest syndrome says parents feel grief & loneliness after their child eventually moves out of their house. -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 10 of 30 / search: "parents child eventually"; 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 19 of 59 / search: "parents child eventually"; 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 20 of 59 / search: "parents child eventually"
- The status quo bias is the tendency to avoid actions that lead to change - instead preferring to maintain normalcy. -> Local sources: 01-All-Uworld-Files.pdf / Question 2 of 30 / search: "bias tendency lead"
